  65. Median Arcuate Ligament Syndrome
    Monica Owerczuk
    Dr. Saker

    Also known as celiac artery compression syndrome. The median arcuate ligament is a fibrous arch that unites the left and right diaphragmatic crura. It usually passes superior to the celiac axis. The MAL may cause external celiac axis compression. Classic findings include luminal stenosis, post-stenotic dilatation, and collateral vessel formation.

  69. Gynecomastia in Male Adolescent
    Randy Miles
    Martha Saker

    Gynecomastia or male breast enlargement is a not uncommon finding, which demonstrates a trimodal age distribution including neonatal, pubertal, and elderly patients. The most common presenting symptoms are breast tenderness, mobile breast lump, or generalized swelling. Findings can be unilateral or bilateral. Bilateral cases are typically asymmetric, seen in 70% of cases. Typical ultrasound imaging features include presence of subareolar circumscribed mass with undulating margins without posterior acoustic shadowing. Finger- like projections can be seen in late disease representing fibrous dendritic changes. Hyperechoic tissue in diffuse glandular pattern can also be seen with late disease. Our patient demonstrated chronic, asymmetric bilateral breast findings consistent with gynecomastia. The ultrasound features were not particularly worrisome for neoplasm or abscess. There was no evidence of posterior accoustic shadowing or spiculated margins to suggest neoplasm. Addionally there wa...

    Access: public

  127. Extrarenal Wilms' Tumor
    Erin Happ
    Jackson Norman, MD

    23 year old female presented to OSH with complaints of abdominal pain,bloating, fever and vaginal discharge. She underwent CT examination where a large, cystic mass was seen originating in the right hemipelvis. Biopsy proved this lesion to be extrarenal Wilms tumor. Extrarenal Wilms is extremely rare and can arise from other neoplasms, namely teratomas. Staging is similar to intrarenal Wilms. Cystic extrarenal Wilms reportedly have a better prognosis than the solid types, however overall extrarenal Wilms is said to have poor prognostic outcomes due to delay in patient presentation.

    Access: public

    Level: Intermediate

  176. Primary Neural Melanoma
    Michael Everton
    Deliah Burrowes, MD

    18 year old male that presented with headache and vomiting. On initial CT was found to have an intraparenchymal hemorrhage in the right medial aspect of the frontal lobe. The initial thought was that this represented a vascular malformation, although a CTA and follow-up angiogram showed no evidence to support this. Patient had a repeat admission for similar complaints with imaging findings once again inconclusive, but given the progression an underlying lesion was considered more likely at this time. Additional imaging showed questionable enhancing nodularity and neurosurgery explored the area, ultimately resecting a mass. On pathology it was diagnosed as primary neural melanoma. An MRI of the spine revealed questionable drop mets in the lumbosacral thecal sac.

    Access: public

    Level: Intermediate

  224. Wandering spleen with torsion
    Rachelle Cruz, D.O.
    James Donaldson, M.D.

    9 year old female with Down's Syndrome presents with mild abdominal pain and constipation. Physical exam demonstrated a firm, nontender mass in the LLQ. Abdominal films demonstrated a markedly dilated stomach with several mildy dilated loops of bowel within the left abdomen. CT showed an ectopically placed, hypoattenuating spleen with swirling of the splenic vessels highly suspicious for splenic torsion secondary to a wandering spleen.

  268. Congenital Central Hypoventilation Syndrome with associated Neuroblastoma.
    Erin Happ
    Francis Prendergast

    A 16 month old male with known Congenital Central Hypoventilation Syndrome and associated Hirschprungs presented to an outside hospital with seizure activity. At that time an MRI of the brain, abdomen and pelvis was performed. A large mass was found in the right upper abdomen, and biopsy was taken. Pathology confirmed neuroblastoma. CCHS is characterized by alveolar hypoventilation and autonomic dysregulation. PHOX2B gene mutation is required for diagnosis of CCHS. Normal genotype is 20/20 with multiple genotypes produced ranging from 20/24 to 20/33. Knowledge of the specific PHOX2B mutation can aid can predict disease severity and comorbidities.

    Access: public

    Level: Intermediate

  330. SPR Unknown #49 -- FINAL
    Erin Happ
    Francis Prendergast

    A 16 month old male with known Congenital Central Hypoventilation Syndrome and associated Hirschprungs presented to an outside hospital with seizure activity. At that time an MRI of the brain, abdomen and pelvis was performed. A large mass was found in the right upper abdomen, and biopsy was taken. Pathology confirmed neuroblastoma. CCHS is characterized by alveolar hypoventilation and autonomic dysregulation. PHOX2B gene mutation is required for diagnosis of CCHS. Normal genotype is 20/20 with multiple genotypes produced ranging from 20/24 to 20/33. Knowledge of the specific PHOX2B mutation can aid can predict disease severity and comorbidities.

    Access: public

    Level: Intermediate

  399. Hypertrophic Osteoarthropathy, secondary to acute cellular rejection
    Christopher Reilly
    Richard Shore

    Hypertrophic osteoarthropathy (HOA) is defined by the findings of clubbing of the digits, periostitis of the long bones, and arthritis. Recently, this syndrome has been linked to acute cellular rejection episodes in children. A case of intestinal transplant with acute cellular rejection and HOA is shown.
